GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.826v - 2.452x³ - 0.413·log(|v| + 1) + 0.340·sin(t)**

The GT has these basis functions:
1. **v** (linear in v)
2. **x³** (cubic in x)
3. **log(|v| + 1)** (logarithmic in |v|)
4. **sin(t)** (sinusoidal in t)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Key observations about GT structure:**
- The v-dependence involves both a linear term `v` and `log(|v|+1)` — these are linearly independent
- The x-dependence is purely `x³`
- The t-dependence is purely `sin(t)`
- No exponential decay/growth in t (no `exp(c*t)` terms unless coefficient is 0)

For candidates with `exp(c*t)` terms: we can set the coefficient to 0, BUT then we lose the sin(t) or cos(t) that might be multiplied with it. So `exp(c5*t)*sin(c6*t)` can become `sin(t)` only if c5=0.

Wait — if c5=0, then `exp(0)*sin(c6*t) = sin(c6*t)`, which works! Similarly `exp(c*t)*cos(c*t+c)` with the exp coefficient set to 0 gives `cos(c*t+c)` which can match `sin(t)`.

Now let me check each candidate for having the right basis functions:

**The critical requirement:** The candidate must be able to produce:
- A `log(|v|+1)` term (or equivalent)
- A `v` term
- An `x³` term  
- A `sin(t)` term

Let me scan for candidates that have a log term or something that can produce `log(|v|+1)`:

Looking through all candidates... Most candidates lack any logarithmic dependence on v. The GT requires `log(|v|+1)`, which is a very specific nonlinear function of v.

Candidates with v-dependence that could potentially match `log(|v|+1) + linear_v`:
- `v*|v|` — this is `v²·sign(v)`, not equivalent to log
- `v³` — cubic, not equivalent to log
- `v/(c+|v|)` — rational, not equivalent to log
- `Max(0,v)` and `Max(0,-v)` — piecewise linear, not log
- `v/sqrt(c+v²)` — not log
- `log(c*exp(c*x)+1)` — this is in x, not v

None of the candidates contain `log(|v|+...)` or any logarithmic function of v.

Let me double-check every candidate for any log term involving v:
- Candidate 7: `log(c3*exp(c4*x)+1)` — in x, not v
- Candidate 10: `log(c3*x²+c4*v²+1)` — this is `log(x²+v²+1)`, not `log(|v|+1)`
- Candidate 15: `log(c8*exp(c9*x)+1)` — in x, not v
- Candidate 33: `log(c3*x²+c4*v²+1)` — same issue as 10

None have `log(|v|+1)`. Since `log(|v|+1)` is linearly independent from all polynomial, rational, exponential, and piecewise-linear functions of v, no candidate can match the GT.

Let me verify: Could `v·|v|` plus `v` somehow equal `log(|v|+1) + linear_v`? No — `v·|v|` is a smooth odd function that grows quadratically, while `log(|v|+1)` grows logarithmically. They are fundamentally different.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** contains the necessary `log(|v|+1)` basis function, and no combination of the available basis functions can reproduce it.
